Jiangda Cross-Country Race: National Central University Wins Double Championship; Team: 1st Central, 2nd Fudan, 3rd Jinan, 4th Chih Chih, 5th Daxia; Individual: 1st Central, Lin Xuan, 15 minutes 18.4 seconds; Central Wins All-Around Title, Guanghua Second

(Nanjing, 4th) The Jiangda cross-country race started at 3:00 PM on the 4th in front of Zhonghua Girls' High School on Baotai Street, Nanjing, passing through Shi Miao Kou, Gaoloumen, heading west along Central Party Headquarters Road, south through Shiziqiao, directly to Gulou Arch, the west side gate of Jinling University, circling the playground once, and ending. The entire course was approximately 4,000 meters. Because the road surface was uneven and the section around Hongwu Gate had too many twists and turns, which could easily lead to problems, the judges decided after a meeting to temporarily shorten the course to over 4,000 meters. The Central team has balanced talent and strong strength. Especially noteworthy was champion Lin Xuan's effort to sprint ahead of Jinan University's Zhou Kewu in the final 50 meters. Individual rankings: (1) Lin Xuan (Central), (2) Zhou Kewu (Jinan), (3) Chen Xingpei (Daxia), (4) Yang Chengxie (Fudan). Time: 15 minutes 18 and 2/5 seconds.

(1) Central Total: 70 points. Champion: Central Team. Lin Xuan 1 point, Wang Dayao 5 points, Gong Jialu 11, Bao Heqing 10, Liu Guangxin 21, Jiang Lianggui 23, total 70 points.

(2) Fudan Total: 95 points. Fudan Team: Lan Shijie 6 points, Yang Wuxie 4 points, Dong Hecheng 9 points, Xu Yongqi 18 points, Zeng Qingzhong 24, Luo Luxin 34 points, total 95 points.

(3) Jinan Total: 132 points. Jinan Team: Zhou Kewu 2 points, Xu Pisheng 28 points, Liu Yibi 14 points, Lu Songya 26 points, Ma Shaobang 35 points, Li Yaoyun 27 points, total 132 points.

(4) Chih Chih Total: 125 points. Chih Chih Team: Huang Chunfang 8 points, Wu Kui 12 points, Sun Lingxian 19 points, Chen Xingchu 32 points, Shen Rongbao 39 points, Zhao Shiji 42 points, total 152 points.

(5) Daxia Total: 159 points. Daxia Team: Chen Xingpei 3 points, Zhou Songzan 17 points, Chen Zhiyuan 20 points, Xie Songpei 38 points, Xu Shouqiang 40 points, Peng Shuxin 41 points, total 159 points.

A Stunning Performance Before Departure: Philippine Chinese Basketball Team Defeats Donghua; Donghua Starts Strong But Gradually Weakens; Philippine Chinese Team Has Strong Stamina, Winning 52-38

The Philippine Chinese basketball team, since returning from the National Games, has had mixed results in Shanghai. Last night's final game against Donghua (i.e., Shanghai University) was initially predicted to be an easy win for Donghua. In the first half, Donghua was indeed very strong, leaving the Philippine Chinese team at a loss. However, in the second half, the Philippine team made a surprising comeback, unstoppable, causing Donghua to look at each other in dismay and confusion. As a result, the Philippine Chinese team won 52-38. Referee: Zhou Jiaqi.

Scheduled Departure to Xiamen

The team's competition schedule in Shanghai has ended. Initially, they planned to arrange a few more games with Western teams, but due to difficulties in arranging matches, the idea was abandoned. Many of the team's players are from Fujian, and the sports community in Xiamen has specifically invited them to compete there. Forward Yang Shufang had already gone to Xiamen, so she did not participate in the Shanghai games. The entire team is scheduled to leave Shanghai for Xiamen on the 9th.

A Summary

The Philippine Chinese team returned to China to participate in the National Games, initially defeating Jiangsu and then losing to Nanjing. In four games in Shanghai, they won three and lost one. Last night's victory over Donghua can be called a masterpiece and a glorious farewell. In total, in six games, the team scored 239 points and conceded 199 points. Star forward Yang Shufang returned to Shanghai from the National Games and immediately went south with the Fujian athletes, unable to compete in Shanghai. Otherwise, the results would have been even more impressive. The results of each game are as follows:

(1) Victory over Jiangsu Team 47-23 National Games

(2) Loss to Nanjing Team 19-37 National Games

(3) Victory over Daxia University 51-24 Friendly Match

(4) Loss to Jinan University 25-34 Friendly Match

(5) Victory over Qianghua Team 45-43 Friendly Match

(6) Victory over Donghua Team 52-38 Friendly Match

Donghua's Initial Strength

At the start of yesterday's game, Donghua was extremely strong, overwhelming, as if entering an empty territory. The defense was tight, the forwards shot accurately, and the whole team worked very systematically. Qian Jingyong aimed accurately and acted nimbly, rarely missing a shot. Wu Guolin and Feng Nianhua each made contributions, finding opportunities on both sides, and everything went smoothly. Under great threat, the Philippine Chinese team almost completely lost its ability to resist, the formation became chaotic, and they were exhausted. The score was first 11-0, then 22-4. Donghua was far ahead, and the Philippine Chinese team's spirits were low, seeming doomed to defeat.

A Surprising Comeback

Faced with this major setback, the Philippine Chinese team was greatly shocked and requested a timeout to reorganize their ranks. From then on, the Philippine Chinese team suddenly made a surprising comeback, launching a fierce counterattack, shedding their weak and chaotic state and transforming into an orderly and energetic force. Zhang Liangxiong made several shots, and Lin Aoliu refused to give up. From then on, the team's morale was greatly boosted, and they became unstoppable. The score rose like a rocket, gradually approaching. At this point, Donghua seemed like the initial Philippine Chinese team, unable to defend on all sides and busy parrying. After scoring 26 points, they stopped there, only seeing the Philippine Chinese team rise step by step, accumulating 23 points. At the end of the first half, Donghua led by only three points.

Tense Situation

As the second half began, the competition intensified. Wu Guolin opened the scoring, adding two points. Lin Aoliu and Zhang Liangxiong responded with two baskets each, adding four points, making it 28-27. Donghua called a timeout to find another way out. Sun Baoqing quietly maneuvered, and Wu Guolin shot accurately from a distance, adding four points, making the situation seem optimistic again. However, the Philippine Chinese team was not willing to be outdone. What was lost quickly was regained easily. Lin Aoliu and Xu Zeyao continued to add two baskets, refusing to let go. The score was still only one point apart: Donghua 32, Philippine Chinese 31.

Sudden Overtaking

At this critical juncture, although Donghua still had the advantage, the score was so close that it was clear that the Philippine Chinese team was gaining momentum. Donghua was in a precarious situation, with danger on all sides. Sure enough, in an instant, Yang Shuhui shot from afar, hitting the target. The Philippine Chinese team suddenly overtook with a score of 33-32. From then on, their momentum grew stronger, and their skills became more refined. They charged left and right, succeeding everywhere. Lin Dengru jumped and threw under the basket, rarely missing. At this point, Donghua's formation became increasingly chaotic, like a plate of scattered sand, beyond recovery. In the end, Donghua lost 38-52.

Scott Cup Preliminary Round: Donghua Defeats West Merchant 7-0; Jinan Draws with Wovesse 1-1; Italian Navy Defeats Saga 4-0; Youyou vs. Lax Today

Yesterday, in two Scott Cup preliminary round matches, Donghua defeated West Merchant team 7-0 in a seemingly effortless match. The current West Merchant team is mediocre and weak. Jinan drew 1-1 with Wovesse. Jinan's offense was very strong, but the left inside forward and left winger were slightly lacking, repeatedly missing opportunities, resulting in an initial 1-0 deficit. In the last five minutes, thanks to Luo Haiguang's pass, Fu Jiang Qiu Zhenglun redeemed himself by scoring a goal, resulting in a draw. In another match, the Italian Navy defeated Saga 4-0. Today at 3:00 PM, Youyou will play against Lax in the Scott Cup match at the Chinese baseball field. The details are as follows.

Donghua Overcomes West Merchant: Wins by Seven Goals; Becomes a One-Sided Battle

This is Donghua's first match in this year's Scott Cup, facing West Merchant. In the 90-minute match, Donghua dominated completely, with a final score of 7-0. Referee:

Donghua Team:

Wan Xianghua

Li Ning, Tu Kaiyuan, Chen Hongguang

Zhou Xianyan, Feng Yunyou, Li Yichen

Guan Xun'an, Wu Youliang, Cao Qiuting

Jia Youliang

West Merchant Team:

Fa Pansi

Ke Lisi, Bo Qisi, Jin Bo

Gao Jin, Xue Fu Han Si

Fa Ping, Mo Lai, Han Tele

Bo Shito

Analysis of the Two Teams

Donghua's lineup is slightly different from the previous year. Chen Yutian, Bu Ye, and Chen Jiaqiu have withdrawn, so Cao Qiuting was selected, and Jia Youliang was invited. The internal personnel are completely the same as before. Yesterday's performance of the team showed a solid defense as always, with ample offensive vigor but insufficient strength. Given time, they should be even more impressive. West Merchant S.F.C. is lacking in talent, and the situation is getting worse. Forwards Hans and Jin Bo can barely cope. The goalkeeper is average, Fa Ping is acceptable, but the rest are not worth mentioning. However, their persistent effort and fighting spirit are commendable.

Offside Nullification

West Merchant met the challenge head-on. Within the first ten minutes, Donghua clearly gained the upper hand. Wan Xianghua made two passes, but Cao and Jia failed to connect properly, missing good opportunities. Li Yichen's powerful shot from 20 yards went straight into the net, but it was ruled offside. Subsequently, Cao Qiuting followed Wan's pass, preparing to shoot, but it was also stopped by the offside whistle. The judgment of offside must be precise, otherwise, both players and spectators will be uneasy.

Three Consecutive Goals

Twenty minutes passed in the blink of an eye. Jia Youliang passed from the right, and West Merchant's defense was lax. Li Yichen opened the scoring with a shot. West Merchant slightly rallied, but any progress was unfavorable. Soon, there was a change in the rear, and another crisis emerged. After Wan passed the defender, Jia kicked the ball onto Qiuting's leg, and it bounced into the goal, making it 2-0. Five minutes later, Cao Qiuting charged like a horse into a plain, advancing through the center line, past the inner defense, and making a solo attack. The opponents were unprepared and dismayed, allowing him to score, making the score 3-0 at halftime.

Scoring Seven Goals

At the beginning of the second half, West Merchant planned to recover lost ground with one effort, but ultimately they lacked the strength to achieve their goals. After fifteen minutes, West Merchant's defense collapsed, leading to an unstoppable series of goals. Li Yichen received a pass from Jia and shot, making it one of the most beautiful and crisp shots of the day. With a 4-goal lead, Donghua's offense became even stronger. Subsequently, Li Yichen, Wan Xianghua, and Cao Qiuting each scored a goal, resulting in a final score of 7-0.

Jinan Draws with Wovesse: 1-1; Jinan Relies on Last-Minute Effort

The Scott Cup match between Jinan and Wovesse was held at the Chinese baseball field, with 3-4,000 spectators. Jinan conceded a goal at the start of the second half. Thanks to efforts in the last five minutes, Qiu Zhenglun redeemed himself by scoring a goal, resulting in a 1-1 draw.

Jinan Team Lineup:

Qiu Zhenglun

Gu Shangxiang, Yun Feng, Wu Shufen

Xu Heng, Xu Yahui, Luo Haiguang

Lai Zuorong, Chen Zhenxiang, Zhang Hongzao

Mei Hongbao

Wovesse Team Lineup:

Jones

Dalahei, Weldon, A Qiao

Hebart, Da Smith Mao Lin

Eagledon P Smith Li Que Shi

Shepart

Review of Both Sides

Jinan's ability to achieve a draw can be described as a pleasant surprise. In the first half, Jinan's offense was very strong, but many shots were too high, frequently missing opportunities. Gu Shangxiang and Xu Yahui balanced offense and defense, and their tireless effort made them key players for the team. Xu Heng's goalkeeping was steady and extraordinary, saving many dangerous shots. The right side of the front line was acceptable, but the left side was too weak, repeatedly missing opportunities. Wovesse was exceptionally strong and tough, with a solid defense and fierce forwards, truly a formidable team.

Minor Contact

Referee Li Nuos sounded the start. Wovesse kicked off and attacked first, Jinan pressed forward, but their plan did not succeed. Qiu Ba was eager to try, repeatedly probing. Jinan occasionally showed a lack of coordination. Gu Shangxiang covered all aspects, rejecting all comers, and all attacks were blocked. At one point, Wovesse was awarded a free kick 40 yards from the goal. "Second in charge" Smith took the kick, and Jones attempted to sneak through, but retreated for offside. Jinan's Qiu Zhenglun's forward progress was blocked. Xu Yahui responded with a long shot from 30 yards. The ball was like a flying arrow, slightly high and ineffective.

Frequent Misses

Wovesse failed to capitalize on two corner kicks from the right wing. Yahui led the team to attack, and Eagledon kicked the ball in the wrong direction, landing in front of the goal. Wu Shufen slipped and fell, losing the opportunity. Mei Hongbao rose from the east, and Luo Haiguang shot again, slightly high and ineffective. Later, he received a pass from Little Mei and attempted a side hook shot. The ball was very fast, but slightly high by an inch, ultimately unsuccessful.

Numerous Scares

Wovesse, repeatedly besieged, attempted a counterattack. Jones launched two attacks, blocked by Carbon-Brother Zhenxiang, and was unable to do anything. Little Mei passed a high ball again, landing on the side of the goal. The position in front of the goal was empty, and it seemed that the fortress could be captured at any moment. Unexpectedly, Qiu Zhenglun was distracted and panicked, shooting wide. The audience sighed at this. In the rear, another emergency arose. Barbarian horses galloped across the border, disrupting Jinan's rear. Shepart swept across, as if in an empty land. Xu Heng wanted to advance but stopped. Mao Lin took advantage of the situation and shot, causing a scare. Fortunately, the ball flew behind the goal, averting danger, but it was still a great fright.

Fall of the City Gate

Jones did not give up his ambition and invaded again, riding the waves and advancing like a broken bamboo. The troops in the center followed closely, surrounding the city gate. Xu Heng, like a flying general, descended from the sky, grabbed the baby and averted the danger. Afterwards, Jones fired another shot, Xu Heng dived to save it. The first half ended without success. As the second half began, the soldiers revealed a stronger offense, Jinan was attacked from all sides, and the crisis was everywhere. Xu Yahui defended alone, busy parrying. Over time, Mao Lin scored a goal from the crowd, rolling the ball into the goal.

Heaven Doesn't Help

After Jinan conceded the goal, the entire army was greatly roused, determined to retaliate. Luo Haiguang received the ball and rushed forward, passing the defense, ready to shoot. Wovesse's goalkeeper, Hebart, saw the opportunity and stepped forward to block it. The two collided head-on, falling to the ground. Zhang Hongzao rushed up to shoot again but was blocked. Unfortunately, after this collision, Haiguang suffered too much shock on his foot and was unable to walk at the time. After a brief massage, he re-entered the field. Mei Hongbao dodged the enemies, passing the ball in front of the goal. Zhang Hongzao rushed up and headed the ball, hitting it squarely, but the ball bounced back off the crossbar. It can be said that heaven didn't help. Subsequently, they were awarded a free kick 20 yards from the enemy's goal. Yahui kicked fiercely, the ball landed and shot towards the goal, the goalkeeper dived and pushed it out, Wu Shufen picked the ball up and passed it forward, Little Mei headed it again and it bounced back. Another failed opportunity, a series of failures.

Redeem the Guilt

Luo Haiguang, unable to walk due to foot pain, switched positions with Xu Yahui, launching a desperate all-or-nothing attack. They fought like a trapped beast, creating a formidable momentum. The heavily fortified Wovesse could not avoid occasional lapses. Haiguang intercepted the enemy's ball in the center, passing it forward. Amid the chaos, Qiu Zhenglun, who had not yet made any contributions, fired a shot amid the noise of the crowd, hitting the target, redeeming his guilt, truly a lucky general. Jinan was like a fish finding water, forming a 1-1 tie. Five minutes later, the game ended. Carbon-Brother Xiang was injured and left the field in the last two minutes.

The National Games Preparatory Committee to Conclude at the End of the Month, with Total Expenditure Exceeding 130,000 Yuan. The Central Stadium to be Returned to the Mausoleum.

(Nanjing, 4th) Zhang Jiong, Director of the Social Affairs Department of the Ministry of Education, stated that the National Games Preparatory Committee will convene its final meeting in mid-month to discuss the closing date. The preparatory committee can be dissolved at the end of the month. The total expenditure for the National Games exceeded 130,000 yuan. Apart from the government-approved funds and ticket revenue of over 20,000 yuan, there is a deficit of over 30,000 yuan. A request will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for assistance or a subsidy from the Ministry of Education to make up for the shortfall. The Central Stadium will be handed back to the Mausoleum Committee for takeover at the end of the month. The newly added equipment in the stadium will be temporarily kept by the Ministry of Education.

In the International Mechanical Movement Competition, Fu Baolu Won the Second Place in Group A

In the International Mechanical Movement Competition hosted by the Russian Overseas Chinese Youth Association in this city on the 3rd of this month, more than 40 foreign athletes from various countries participated. Among the Chinese participants, there was only Fu Baolu. The competition was divided into Group A and Group B, with three winners selected in each group. Mr. Fu won the second place in Group A with a score of 191 points, only one point behind the record of 192 points set by Mr. Deqi, a Russian who won the championship. Mr. Fu ranked second by a margin of one point. During the competition, Fu was particularly skilled in the three events of horizontal bar, parallel bars, and rings. The spectators marveled at the agility of his movements and the dangerousness of the scenes. He is truly a promising talent. Mr. Fu currently works at the Diligence Bookstore at No. 392 Father Laois Road in this city and is the holder of this year's National Games pole vault championship.

Out-of-Town

Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, Zhou Fohai, Inspects Education in Northern Jiangsu Again. Visits Schools in Shaobo Town. Stops the Boat at Zhaoguan Dam for Inspection.

(Zhenjiang Correspondence) Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, in order to thoroughly understand the educational situation in the province and promote the progress of local education, personally went to the north and south of the Yangtze River last winter and this spring to inspect education. The situation was reported in various newspapers. Now that the current semester has been underway for a long time, whether the agencies and schools in various regions have earnestly followed and implemented the decrees and various plans issued by the department needs to be examined. In addition to the provincial inspectors going to various places for detailed guidance, on the morning of November 1st at 7 o'clock, he took the Jialu patrol ship from Zhenjiang to Hua Yang area for inspection. Accompanying him were Chen Xifang, the head of the Second Division, Xiang Jutan, the head of the Third Division, Yi Junzuo, the director of compilation and review, and Tian Yuelong, the director of general affairs. At 1 PM, he arrived at Shaobo Town and went ashore to visit the Shaobo Elementary School of Jiangdu County. The school has four grades. Director Zhou and others inspected the teaching one by one, examined the report cards, and inquired about the daily management of the school and the teaching situation of the teachers and staff in detail. He gave concrete guidance on the cleanliness of the school, correcting student assignments, recording reports, and teaching methods. The inspection lasted two hours before it was completed. Then he returned to the ship and drove north. Passing the Zhaoguan Dam, because it was related to water conservancy in northern Jiangsu, he specially stopped the ship for inspection. Along the way, the weather was clear and the scenery was beautiful. Whenever Director Zhou passed through villages and towns, he would go out of the cabin to browse, paying attention to the living conditions of farmers and the national historical sites related to virtue and resistance to foreign aggression, such as the Yangzi Bridge and the Lujin Temple. At 6:30 PM, he arrived at Gaoyou. It is reported that he will go ashore to inspect the self-study of high school students in the county.

When it is necessary to ask for leave and has been approved, they must also consult with the principal and ask someone to take their positions, but the time limit must not exceed one month, so as to value their responsibilities, etc. It is specially ordered that the departments and bureaus forward the notice to the public and private high schools and above under their jurisdiction for information.

Various Schools Hold Speech Contests During the Anti-Banditry Propaganda Week. The Municipal Education Bureau Issued the Contest Regulations Yesterday. The Contests Will be Held Separately in Various Schools on the 10th of this Month.

The Anti-Banditry Movement Propaganda Week in this city is scheduled to be held from the 6th to the 11th of this month, and it is stipulated that the 5th day will be the day for elementary and secondary schools in the city to hold anti-banditry speech contests. The Municipal Education Bureau specially issued the contest regulations yesterday and ordered various schools to hold them separately. The details are as follows:

Circular to All Schools: The letter from the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang stated that the first discussion meeting of the Shanghai Anti-Banditry Propaganda Week Preparatory Committee decided that the Education Bureau would organize the speech contest and must be held on November 10. The record is on file. Accordingly, it is hereby communicated. I hope you will check and handle it accordingly. Accordingly, the speech contest should be conducted by schools at all levels after receiving the document, and students should be solicited to follow the "Anti-Banditry Propaganda Week Anti-Banditry Speech Contest Regulations for Elementary and Secondary Schools" issued by this bureau and held in their respective schools. It is also hoped that the situation at that time will be filled in the report form and submitted to the bureau. In addition to the separate order, a copy of the regulations is issued for compliance. This order,

Contest Regulations: (1) In order to enable citizens of the city to deeply understand the scourge of the Red Bandits and to be determined to eradicate them together, it is specially designated from November 6th to November 11th as Anti-Banditry Propaganda Week. Schools at all levels must hold anti-banditry speech contest meetings in their respective schools on the fifth day (i.e., November 10th). (2) After receiving the notice, schools at all levels should immediately solicit students to register and participate. (3) The topic of the speech contest should be within the scope of exterminating the Red Bandits. (4) The judges of the contest should be three judges invited by the schools from scholars outside the school or teachers of the school, but at least one person must be from outside the school. (5) The judging criteria are: ideological content accounts for 30%, structure accounts for 25%, language and tone account for 25%, and attitude and posture account for 20%. (6) When holding the contest, each school should suspend classes for half a day, and all students in the school should be present to listen. If there are special circumstances, it may also be held during the spare time of the day. (7) Schools at all levels must fill in each item in the report form issued by the Education Bureau according to the situation on the day and report it within three days. (8) The Education Bureau will compile the names of the first-place winners with excellent results in the contest of each school and disclose them in the newspaper, and send a letter to the Municipal Party Department to issue winning prizes.

Free Talk

Believing Everything in Books

— Tang Tao

We Chinese believe in books the most, but our Chinese books are the least trustworthy.

For example, when talking about heroes, it is definitely not enough to only talk about being straightforward and liking to help the oppressed. One must be able to soar into the clouds, have a white light on their finger, and also chase after people to kill them; if one encounters an opponent and is defeated, one must not die at the critical moment. Therefore, there will be enlightened monks to save them. Who gives the tip? It is said: "A sudden whim."

This seems too absurd to be believed, but it is not; in addition to roasting one's hands like sugar-fried chestnuts in hot yellow sand, there are even people who abandon their hometown, do not bring a penny with them, and prepare to fly to Wudang Mountain to learn swordsmanship from Taoists and monks.

We Chinese live under such thoughts.

However, "wise men" must object again. Because these books are not orthodox after all, and most of these people are also simple-minded. "Upper-class" and "higher-class" Chinese would not do this. But hold on, let me give you a few examples: (Zhuangzi's Xiaoyao You) In the North Sea, there is a fish, its name is Kun. The Kun is so big that no one knows how many thousands of miles it is. It transforms into a bird, its name is Peng. The back of the Peng is so big that no one knows how many thousands of miles it is. When it gets angry and flies, its wings are like clouds hanging from the sky.

(Historical Records) Gaozu drunkenly walked in the swamp, and a large snake blocked the path in front of him, so he drew his sword and chopped it off. An old woman cried at the place at night, saying: "My son is the son of the White Emperor. Now he is killed by the son of the Red Emperor."

These two books can probably be regarded as orthodox, right? But why are some of them like nonsense? A fish is so big that it is thousands of miles long and can also turn into a bird; the son of an old woman is a snake, but suddenly he is said to be the son of the White Emperor. What is going on here? "Wise men" believe it deeply without doubting it.

It must be said again that ancient books are not enough to restrain modern people. In fact, among modern people, especially among talented modern people, untrustworthiness still exists. For example, someone says that the tip of a woman's tongue is the tail of a gecko, then the tail of a gecko is the tip of a woman's tongue; if someone actually hugs the tail of a gecko to kiss, that's terrible!

Untrustworthy, untrustworthy, but I am afraid that there are still people who will believe it.

Famous quotes should not be missed, so let me add another one.

"The river is like a standing coffin."

How should such a treasure be viewed? Fortunately, it is a talented young poet. But this time, many people have been fooled. The poor cannot survive, so they throw themselves into the river, thinking that they will be safely coffined and their bodies will be spared from exposure. But soon they float up like dead pigs.

I don't want to advise people to write fewer famous poems and articles, but I hope everyone will not believe too much in them. Books are not entirely reliable.

Reliable books are not easy to exist!

About the "Berlin China Art Exhibition"

— Fu Yiye

Four months ago, I wrote a short article for the Chinese art exhibition to be held in Berlin, the capital of Germany, next spring. At that time, the art exhibition was just beginning to be prepared, but I overestimated myself and put forward three opinions: First, in terms of the collection of artworks, it should be publicly solicited from writers across the country, so that the quantity and quality of the works can be rich and perfect. Second, among the products of the ancient, modern, and contemporary periods, emphasis should be placed on the contemporary part. At least half of the works of contemporary writers should be included. Of course, ancient and modern paintings are better than contemporary ones. This only increases the artistic evaluation, and the current stage of Chinese art and the development of the entire art movement in the future actually rely on contemporary works to peek into and infer. The last opinion is that I hope that our artists will change the unpromising habit of being addicted to ancient things and the escapist ideas of pretentious literati, absorb modern colors in terms of painting materials, and create something with a sense of the times. If we continue to stick to the old rules and the paintings are still religious images of gods and Buddhas, figures in corner scarves and square hats, and buildings of wild temples and thatched houses, if we take this kind of thing to meet foreigners, people will suspect that China is still stuck in the Jin and Tang dynasties! That article was sent to a newspaper supplement in this city that talks about beauty and taste relatively, but maybe the article is not beautiful enough to be tasteful, or the manuscript is not a personal introduction of a considerable figure, so it was thrown into the wastebasket by the editor.

Now, seeing the news that the members of the art exhibition committee are going abroad on the one hand; on the other hand, Wang Qi, Gao Ailin, and others have raised questions, and today's Shen Bao also carries the suggestions of the preparatory committee members Lin Fengmian, Lin Wenzheng, and Qi Baishi to the preparatory committee. In this way, I feel that the article thrown into the editor's wastebasket is not useless after all. After moving the past opinions here, let's look at the development of this event.

Looking at the document presented by Wang Qi, Gao Ailin, and others to the Ministry of Education, it clearly accuses Liu Haisu personally of monopolizing the matter, so the collection of works is limited to a small number of writers in Shanghai, and they are not excellent works. Whether this is the case in fact, we outsiders will not know, but since there has been no public solicitation or exhibition during the preparatory period, it is inevitable to have such doubts, but even the preparatory committee members Lin Qi and others do not know that the committee members are going abroad (see the Shen Bao on the 11th). Because of other people's grievances, the three suggestions came. This is really confusing. Originally, those three suggestions should have been paid attention to when the preparations began. At this time, a second solicitation is made. Can this short time achieve "universal solicitation", then "collect widely" and "select in detail" to "strive for perfection"? A contract for more than two years and a preparatory committee established for half a year, but the solicitation of art exhibition works still has to be done at the last minute. What is the inside story after all? Let's wait for the parties involved to answer!

"Pseudonym" and "Beautiful Name"

— Yu Shixia

Literati in the Ming Dynasty liked to use aliases, called Taoist names. At that time, Taoism was flourishing, and there were many lecturers. The establishment of Taoist names was to cater to the public and show respect, which is what is meant by "scholars are called so-and-so sir." And those who are flattering and vile also use it to please those they respect, from humble and vulgar scholars to prominent celebrities and nobles, all have Taoist names. Someone once wrote a poem saying:

Mencius' name was Ke, but he did not say his nickname. Now, Taoist names are numerous.

The cuckoo is originally a famous yang bird, but people want to call it a cuckoo.

As for today, capable writers like to use uncommon pseudonyms, and one person has as many as a dozen pseudonyms. I have presumptuously speculated on the reason for this, not that they do not like fame, but to escape their literary fame; not that they fear debate, but to escape their responsibility for words; is it that there are many taboos at the time, and they have no choice but to hide their names? Also, today's movie stars and dancers like to use reduplicated words for their beautiful names. I don't know who started this, but there are more and more followers. Examining the beauties of the Tang Dynasty, many of them used reduplicated words for their beautiful names, such as Yuan Zhen's concubine named Yingying, Zhang Hu's concubine named Yanyan, General Liu's beloved prostitute named Zhenzhen, and Zhang Jianfeng's dancer named Panpan. There were also prostitutes who were good at singing named Haohao, Duanduan, Zhuozhuo, Xixi, the Yang family in Qiantang named Aiai, the Wu family named Saisai, and the Fan family named Yanyan. There was a noble concubine named Yingying in Tianbao. During the Dali period, there were talented people named Zhang Honghong and Xue Qiongqiong. Also, Yang Yuqing's concubine was named Yingying. Only what is mentioned in the Qixiu Leigao, the actual number should be more than this. It should be the fashion of the time, and it has not changed in the Five Dynasties and Song Dynasty. Now, this fashion is popular again among singers and actors. The innovation of literary pseudonyms and the restoration of ancient beautiful names are things that those who collect customs should think deeply about!

A Trip to the Buddhist Kingdom (Continued)

— Ba Jin

After visiting Mount Foding, I didn't see anything strange. I still wanted to go to Pusa Peak to see the sky lanterns, but there was no time. I also needed to meet my friend at the beach, as we had agreed beforehand. I should go down the mountain before the sun sets.

We didn't sleep well that night. People were playing mahjong outside, making a lot of noise for a long time. Later, the tea servers started arguing over tips. It only quieted down late at night. In the morning, before we were awake, the person in the temple who received guests came to knock on our door and wake us up, saying the ship had arrived. After eating breakfast, we followed that person down the mountain. It was very early, only five or six o'clock, but the sun had already risen, and the air was fresh. All along the way, we heard birds singing and saw the green shadows of the trees. As we approached the dock, we heard the steamship's whistle and hurried to the dock, but the ship had already left. We could see the yellow hull, the black smokestack, and the gray-black smoke. Yesterday, someone clearly told us that the ship to Shanghai would pass by here around seven or eight o'clock, but now it was just past six o'clock, and the ship had already left, far away. There was no way for us to catch up. Then, many female pilgrims arrived at the dock in sedan chairs, their luggage carried by porters. They seemed very confident that they wouldn't miss the ship, but in the end, they had to stop there for a while. After saying a lot of complaints, they had the sedan carriers take them back, and the porters carried their luggage back.

Judging from this situation, we were probably never going to have a chance to catch a ship to Shanghai. My friend worked in a factory in Shanghai, and his desire to return was truly like an arrow. I also didn't want to stay on Mount Putuo to see more of the monks' faces. But there was nothing we could do, so we had to return to the temple. This time, it surprised the receptionist monk even more. Later, thanks to him, he figured out a way for us to take a small steamer to Zhoushan. Taking a ship in Zhoushan was very convenient, as there were small steamers leaving for Shanghai every day from there.

We left Putuo at ten o'clock that morning, feeling very relieved, even though we knew we would be staying in Zhoushan for one night. But we had friends there to take care of us, who would provide us with all sorts of conveniences and show us some new and interesting things, things that would at least be more interesting than the monks' faces.

The reason I particularly mention the monks' faces is because there are so many monks on Putuo, everywhere you look. Monks also know how to deal with guests, how to calculate money, how to employ servants, and how to do business, just like ordinary merchants. Temples have guest rooms, which are like hotels in Shanghai. The new facilities are complete, and in addition to the tea servers who serve the guests, there are also receptionists who pick up and drop off guests. The food is vegetarian, but guests can also buy meat dishes and bring them in. Wealthy people can also get all sorts of conveniences here. We once found a opium pipe under the sofa cover in our room. We heard the sound of mahjong tiles, only missing seeing someone calling in prostitutes.

The night before we left Putuo, we had a conversation with the receptionist monk. That monk was fat and had big ears, but he had a clever mind. He spoke beautifully, knew the dialects of several provinces, and was especially good at flattering female pilgrims. What he said to us was very frank. He said, "The temples on Mount Putuo only do business for these few months every year. But the expenses are too high. In the past two years, the competition has been too fierce, and business hasn't been very good, so everyone inevitably loses money. This business is really hard to do, but many monks rely on it for a living, and there's nothing else to do if we don't do it." The meaning was very clear. So, when pilgrims come to their door, they have to fleece them. Doing a Water and Land Dharma Assembly costs at least a thousand dollars. Doing a small Buddhist service costs more than a hundred dollars. But the wives and young ladies of gentlemen don't care at all. I unintentionally saw a Water and Land Dharma Assembly at another temple. I really can't find words to describe how the monks flattered the female pilgrims. Only classical painters could paint their faces in detail.

We received considerable preferential treatment on Mount Putuo. I felt more comfortable in the temple than in a hotel in Shanghai. So, I believe my description doesn't have any bias. When I returned to Shanghai, someone asked me what impressions I brought back. I replied that I had visited a large marketplace, where the goods being traded were Bodhisattvas, and the merchants doing business were super merchants. I myself was just a most ungenerous customer. (The End)

Two Brothers (19)

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

Then, one of those thoughts that often came to him so abruptly, so quickly, that he could neither foresee, nor control, nor change, one of those thoughts that he felt as if it came from another independent and fierce soul, crossed his mind: "Bah! He's too stupid. He won't go and enjoy himself like that. He'll marry that little widow Lu."

He stood up.

"I'll let you dream about your future alone; as for me, I need to take a walk."

He shook hands with his brother, and then said in a very sincere tone:

"Well, my little Zhe'an, you're rich now! I'm very happy to be able to meet you alone tonight, so I can tell you how happy this makes me, how much I congratulate you, and how much I love you."

Gentle and docile Zhe'an was very touched by these words and said falteringly:

"Thank you… thank you… my good Bi'er, thank you."

So Bi'er slowly walked back alone, his cane hanging on his arm, his hands clasped behind his back.

As he walked back to the city, he considered what to do for amusement. He was unable to enjoy his walk fully because he encountered his brother, unable to enjoy the sea view fully, and felt very unhappy.

He suddenly thought: "I'll go to old man Malosco's place for a glass of sweet wine;" so he walked towards the Danguwier district again.

He had met old man Malosco when he was an intern at the public hospitals in Paris. This was an old Polish man who had fled the country for political reasons. According to others, he had been involved in some terrible stories in Poland. He came to France, took another exam, and then practiced his profession as a pharmacist. No one knew anything about his past life, so various legends about him circulated among the interns and externs at the hospital, and later among his neighbors. This reputation of a terrible rebel, nihilist, regicide, and reckless patriot who had miraculously secured his head, stirred Roland Bi'er's adventurous and passionate imagination; therefore, he became good friends with this Polish old man, but he never heard any confessions from him about his previous life. This old man also relied on the young doctor's help to open his business in Havre. He hoped that this new doctor would bring him many customers.

Before this hope was realized, he had to live a simple life in his humble pharmacy, temporarily maintaining his life by doing small business with the small property owners and workers in his district.

Bi'er often went to see him after dinner and sat with him for a long time, because he liked Malosco's quiet face and rare conversation. He felt that his long silences were very meaningful.

Spring and Autumn

A Look at Sports in the Past and Present

— Qian Zuizhu

Sports, in our country, is "what I rely on to exist." For example, the "shooting" and "charioteering" in the "Six Arts" contain the function of tempering the body, just like the current sports. Moreover, "their competition is gentlemanly," showing that people at the time also attached great importance to the morality of sports. Therefore, the talents of that time were both literary and martial. It wasn't until later that the literary and martial paths diverged, resulting in the great harm of "the scholar cannot bind a chicken, and the warrior cannot read."

I remember in my childhood, schools were newly founded, and sports were immature. There were very few events, only knowing a few items such as running, high jump, low hurdles, group exercises, and apparatus exercises. At that time, most of the teachers only knew about sports, not about training. The principals only knew how to encourage students to work hard and show off for the school, without paying attention to the students' physical condition and without asking about daily hygiene. Young people were eager to win, using seven parts of their physical strength to do ten parts of sports. As a result, I don't know how many good students were sacrificed. Every sports meet, I don't know how many tragedies were hidden. (I was one of them, the disease of spitting blood harmed my lifelong career.) It wasn't until the last ten years that this malpractice has been slightly reduced. But there are still those who treat students' lives as a child's play, like this year, when a student from a certain school died in swimming due to the teacher's carelessness. But these are only a few. On the whole, it has indeed entered the right track of sports. The "right eye" for tempering the body has been recognized. It is no longer the sport of young masters and misses, but the activity of brave and healthy youths.

I say this with evidence; just look at the students now, eight out of ten are muscular and strong, and their bones are stretched. It can be seen that they have received average development training on weekdays, so they have this strong harvest. No wonder this time's National Games will create many new records. In short, the previous was a malformed sport of abandoning the root and pursuing the tip, and now it is a basic training of universal development. In the past, it was seven parts of the body doing ten parts of sports. Now it is ten parts of capital doing ten parts of competition. Among the various current situations in the country, it is the only gratifying progress.

Finally, I believe that the people of the country should give a stable life to outstanding talents, such as Liu Changchun and Fu Baolu, so as not to bury heroes. (The report said how pitiful was the cold treatment and neglect that the old athlete Mr. Zhu Ende encountered.) We must be more careful to protect them, so as not to be plotted against. It must be known that there is a deadly enemy around us who does not allow us to have outstanding talents. (There are many previous examples, not only in the field of sports. Many of our country's talents have been victimized by their conspiracies.) So, if we still do not know how to love and protect them, and let them live and die on their own, then the next international sports, not only will we not be able to win, I am afraid that even Mr. Situ's "extreme jump" will not be able to be achieved.

Expectation

— Yongzi

Wang Xiao'er suffered a loss from Zhang Da'gezi, and finally couldn't think of a way to turn the tables. He also didn't have the patience to go to Mount Emei to cultivate and practice hard, in order to prepare for a gentleman's revenge after three years. So he had no choice but to cross his arms and hide in the corner of the door, chanting "Amitabha Buddha" and praying to the Great Compassionate Avalokitesvara and the Savior of Suffering, to bring misfortune to Zhang Da'gezi, so that he would choke to death while eating, fall to his death while walking, drown to death while crossing the bridge, and die of heatstroke in June. After some time, seeing that Zhang Da'gezi didn't even get prickly heat and didn't even sneeze, he changed direction, day and night hoping that Zhang Da'gezi would fight with Scar A'Si on East Street and Jiu'er Mazi on West Street. And what he hoped for even more was that these two heroes would unite to beat Zhang Da'gezi. Two against one. Although Zhang Da'gezi is a hero, he can't avoid a "dog eats mud" moment. When Wang Xiao'er thought of this delightful point, he couldn't help but loosen his crossed arms and slapped his thigh hard, laughing loudly: "Good is rewarded with good, and evil is rewarded with evil, Zhang Da'gezi, you only know how to bully me, Wang Xiao'er, how come you're lying on the ground today, losing face." This is Wang Xiao'er's revenge plan that he thinks about day and night. Although whether Scar A'Si and Jiu'er Mazi will fall out with Zhang Da'gezi, whether they will unite to carry out two against one, and whether Zhang Da'gezi will really play "dog eats mud" are still uncertain when Wang Xiao'er is hiding in the corner of the door, Wang Xiao'er doesn't have any bigger plans other than that.

In society, typical characters like Wang Xiao'er can be found everywhere. Naturally, this is the easiest way to take revenge, which is a hundred times better than going to Mount Emei to cultivate and practice hard for three years before being able to take revenge. Furthermore, if Wang Xiao'er suffered a loss from Zhang Da'gezi and really went to practice martial arts and took revenge, it would seem too obvious, and people would laugh at him for "not being willing to suffer losses." Only by using this "understanding in the stomach" method and sticking to the hope of Zhang Da'gezi playing "dog eats mud," can he not only breathe a sigh of relief, but also say that set of "good is rewarded with good, and evil is rewarded with evil," which means that Yin and Yang have not disappeared, and justice still exists. This is the essence of the philosophy of life.

Chrysanthemum

— Jinlou

It's the season for chrysanthemums again! The beautiful image of cold elegance and no charm floats in my mind!

Indeed, chrysanthemums are very lovable, golden silk chrysanthemums, rouge chrysanthemums, large ink chrysanthemums, as well as Autumn Moon, Feather Rhododendron, Lion's Mane, Coral Hook... what moving names! Their graceful figures, set off by the dark green petals, beckon like beauties in the autumn sunlight, by the bamboo fence, by the pink wall... intoxicating the hearts of so many people?

"Picking chrysanthemums under the east fence, leisurely seeing the South Mountain," since ancient times, Chinese poets, in addition to liking to drink wine and watch the moon, have also had a very good relationship with chrysanthemums! Especially Tao Yuanming, he especially praised the "solitary fragrance in late autumn" of chrysanthemums, so later generations often regarded Tao Yuanming as the only confidant of chrysanthemums. But is it just Tao Yuanming? Since ancient times, poets have all lived in simple lives, yearning for the beauty of elegant nature, so chrysanthemums have never failed to be loved, praised, and chanted by a great poet, even Wang Anshi, who was the most officialistic, also had the line "Yellow chrysanthemum has supreme virtue, solitary fragrance defies the cold." The elegance of chrysanthemums can be seen from this!

However, times have changed now. Writers all take "there is literature only when there is a woman" as their motto, and ordinary new poets are also deeply influenced by the urban materialism of enjoyment, abandoning the acceptance of natural beauty, and plunging into the charming cafes and dance halls night after night, wanting to find their so-called "inspiration" in those white-uniformed waitresses and red-cheongsammed dancers! Therefore, what they chant is either the worship of "curvaceous beauty" or the eulogy of "leg beauty," the thick breath of flesh in it cannot be read. If chrysanthemums have knowledge, recalling those confidants like Tao Yuanming in ancient times, they have all been lost today! How can they not be sad? Everything has its ups and downs, this is probably the chrysanthemum's vicissitudes!

Random Talk on Cartoons

— Qian Yun writes, Wen Dongliang draws

—— Stiff! ——

The man thinks: Among these gifts, no matter which one, it will at least抵me three months' salary; and it will make me broke during these three months, even for movie tickets! But the reality can no longer be delayed, so what to do?

The woman thinks: He keeps saying "I love you," but it's all empty talk every day. No matter which of these gifts, it's the least he should do to show his love; but even this little bit — what if he refuses? Then let's break up.

Young people! Do you think love is all happiness?

Northeast Fourth Company Commander

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18: Secretly Passing Tea, Bearing Sorrow to Comfort the Husband; Hastily Leaving the Frontier, Forcibly Smiling to Bid Farewell to the Family

These few words can also be regarded as his temporary feelings. It can also be said that he is lazy to act, and uses these words to excuse himself. But when these words reached Zhao Ziqiang's ears, his heart stirred. If he is so easily moved by emotion, there will be many more emotions. He pushed open the door and saw my family in the backyard. He wanted to be moved by emotion. Sitting in the house, he used to hear my footsteps passing through the front yard, but in the future, he won't anymore. These are all things he should recall, and it is inevitable that he will be moved by emotion. What can one say about this? Zhao Ziqiang thought of this, and everything was silent. He lowered his head and looked at his leather shoes, kicking the tips of his feet on the ground randomly. Gui Zhi had already poured a cup of tea, and then smiled and brought it to him. She said softly, don't be sad, drink this cup of hot tea. Zhao Ziqiang responded and suddenly stood up, taking his teacup with both hands and said to him: I have many things to say to you, but I can't remember for a moment, which sentence to start with. I am a soldier on active duty, my body belongs to the country, there is only order, no freedom, please forgive me. Gui Zhi smiled: You are overthinking, I didn't say I wouldn't forgive you. Zhao Ziqiang held the teacup, not knowing whether to drink or sit down, just staring blankly at people. Gui Zhi pursed her lips and smiled, for a long, long time, before saying: Don't be so pessimistic, a real man should always do something earth-shattering. Sit down and drink tea, don't think about those things. Zhao Ziqiang heard this, looked at him, and slowly sat down. Unintentionally, he had already moved away from the square stool. When he sat down, he didn't touch the stool. His body swayed, and he was almost about to fall down, but he thought that he was still holding a teacup in his hand, and it should not be broken. If it broke, it would be an ominous sign for the person leaving, so he pinched the cup hard, unwilling to let go, but the hot tea that spilled out of the teacup burned the skin on his hand to a purple color. His right hand really couldn't hold it anymore, so he sent the teacup to his left hand. (231)

Children's Paradise

Several Simple Magic Tricks

— Yin Feng

Sure Success in Guessing

This clever magic trick only requires a alarm clock and a pencil. If you can't find a alarm clock temporarily, you can use a pocket watch or a watch, but it's smaller and harder to see clearly. Now, assuming you are using a alarm clock, show it to the audience, and then ask them to elect one person to think of a number from one to twelve on the clock face, and secretly tell the audience. Then you tell him (that is, the person elected by the audience to think of a number) that: "Now I will use a pencil to tap on the clock face. When you see me tapping on a number, you add one to the number you are thinking of. For example, if you are thinking of six o'clock, then when my pencil taps on one o'clock, you add one and it becomes seven; I tap once, you add once, and when it reaches twenty, you shout stop, and I can know what number you are thinking of." This is very simple, as long as you remember clearly the number of times the pencil taps the numbers on the clock face. Remember the first seven taps, no matter what time the tap lands on, it doesn't matter. The eighth tap must land on twelve o'clock, the ninth tap must land on eleven o'clock, the tenth tap must land on ten o'clock, and so on in that order, until the person thinking of the number has added up to twenty and shouted stop. Then the time on the clock face that your pencil tip has landed on is the number that he is thinking of. It works every time, and you will be right every time.

Moving Coins

First, prepare twelve copper coins, place them on the table, arranged in a square, with four coins on each side; then say to the audience: "There are twelve copper coins here, arranged in a square, with four coins on each side. Now I want to change each side to five copper coins, and it will still be a square. You cannot add or subtract a single copper coin, that is, you can only move the position of the copper coins, but you cannot increase or decrease the number of copper coins. Can the audience do it?" If they say they can't think of it, they can't change it; then you say: "I'll change it for you to see." When changing, you just need to remember the order of the copper coins, that is, from the left hand side to the right hand side, it is the first to the fourth; then from top to bottom, it is the fifth to the seventh; then from right to left, it is the eighth to the tenth; then from bottom to top, it is the eleventh and the twelfth. Remembering the order of the copper coins makes it easy to change. Just move the fifth coin to the fourth coin and place it there; then move the second coin to the first coin and place it there; then move the eleventh coin to the tenth coin and place it there; then move the eighth coin to the seventh coin and place it there; then it becomes a square with five copper coins on each side, only moving the position, without increasing or decreasing the number.

Tying a Handkerchief

Borrow a handkerchief from the audience, and then teach any one of them to take the handkerchief and hold the two opposite corners of the handkerchief; that is, one hand holds one end. Then ask him to tie a knot, but he is not allowed to let go of the hand and loosen the handkerchief corner he is holding. If he doesn't know the secret of this trick, he won't be able to tie it no matter what; because to tie a knot in a handkerchief, you must cross the two corners of the handkerchief, and then turn one corner downwards and inwards to thread it through, in order to tie a knot. Now you are not allowed to let go, you cannot loosen it, and it is impossible to tie a knot. But it is easy for those who know magic. Little friends who want to be little magicians, why not give it a try. Just cross your two wrists over each other and place them in front of your chest, and then teach a viewer to thread one end of the handkerchief through the empty space in front of your chest behind your hands, and you hold it; for example, if your wrists are crossed, your right hand is inside and your left hand is outside, then you grab the end that is threaded through the intersection with your left hand, and hold the corner that is not threaded through with your right hand. Your wrists still have to be crossed and cannot be moved.) At this time, half of the handkerchief is inside and half is outside. Then you hold the two ends of the handkerchief, and pull your wrists back without crossing them, and the handkerchief is tied into a knot. Isn't that a knot tied without letting go of the two handkerchief corners that you are holding?

Call Loan Interest Rate Increases by 0.5 Yuan

This year's call loan interest rate has not been high, and has sometimes been very loose. Therefore, the total amount for the entire month is often less than the original fixed price of 2 yuan. As a result, the daily call loan interest rate is always discounted at 2.95 yuan, like a stereotypical article. However, last month (October) seemed more robust, with the total exceeding 2 yuan. Therefore, the current call loan market price decided by the Money Trade Association's standing committee meeting has been increased by 0.5 yuan, to 2.5 yuan with a discount of 0.95 yuan. However, overdue interest will still be charged at 4.5 yuan. If the interest remains past due, the rate will increase gradually. Thus, October's call loan interest was slightly better, but overdue interest remained the same as in the past.

Majority Expected Increase in US Cotton Estimates

A New York dispatch from November 3rd reports on the cotton market situation for the week, stating that the US government's announcement of entering the global gold market initially caused some buying in raw cotton at the beginning of the week. The market then showed a bright but uneven appearance. Merchants were waiting to see the development of the authorities' gold purchase policy and its impact on prices, as well as waiting for the release of the US cotton production report on November 8th. Private cotton production estimates averaged around 13.5 million bales, so the majority expected the government estimate to be slightly higher than before. This uncertain situation also hindered transactions. At the same time, it was generally believed that the implementation of monetary policy and the general degree of recovery would be the main factors dominating the final cotton price. News from the South indicated that the raw cotton market was tight, as more cotton farmers were visibly accepting loans and signing up for the next season's cotton acreage reduction program than before. Cotton trading was sluggish, but the cloth market remained stable.

Grain

Flour and Wheat Fall with Increasing Momentum

The flour market sentiment is very weak because a considerable amount of foreign wheat has been traded in recent days. Factories have ample stocks, and there are also pre-ordered wheat shipments yet to arrive. Statistics show that their chips are increasing, so major factories are planning to hedge their positions. However, actual sales are sluggish, and they are unable to hoard and hedge. Factories find it difficult to see a large outlet for their flour stocks in the short term. However, if there are more foreign wheat transactions today and tomorrow, the market will need to move downstream. Moreover, the amount of US wheat borrowed on credit is substantial and must be fully collected. At present, only a small number are buying and distributing to various factories. In the future, there must be further inflows and outflows, and the market will need to wait for large companies to digest their stocks before a turnaround can occur. Yesterday, guest sales were very sluggish, and the market fell. The closing price for this month was down 0.0125 yuan, next month was down 0.015 yuan, January was down 0.01 yuan, February was down 0.0075 yuan, March was down 0.0125 yuan, and April was down 0.0175 yuan.

The wheat market opened lower because the market sentiment was extremely weak after a large amount of foreign wheat was traded. Brokers were still trying their best to hedge their positions. Long positions were watching, and short positions were adding to their positions. Short covering was also waiting for a further decline before making inquiries. As a result, the market gradually trended downward, and the afternoon saw a further decline. The closing price for this month was down 0.05 yuan, December was down 0.03 yuan, January was down 0.06 yuan, February was down 0.03 yuan, April was down 0.03 yuan. The city opened with Shandong wheat at 3.8 yuan, second grade at 3.76 yuan, Gao Deng wheat at 3.7 yuan, 3.8 yuan, second grade at 3.75 yuan, and Pudong wheat at 3.45 yuan, for a total of 3,000 bales, which were all taken by Gao Feng.

Du Yangjian was also flat, while the sales of thick rice from Hong Kong and other regions were 1,500-6,000 shi, and the market was slightly tighter, but prices only fluctuated by a few points. Foreign Guest Xiang Rice Sales Halted

Yesterday, the foreign guest xiang rice market was even more sluggish, and guest buyers completely stopped buying. Local sellers seized the opportunity, and prices fell by nearly 0.1 yuan again. The city sold 424 bags of Jiang Si Ji late rice and New Late Rice at 7.67 yuan and Chen Late Rice at 7.55 yuan to the local merchants, all of which were sold to local merchants. Guest buyers were all watching. Fujian already had a large inventory, and Guangdong was directly arranging for loading in Hunan and Anhui provinces, so sales were even more sluggish.

Railway Station Increases Miscellaneous Grain Storage Fees

Grain transported by rail has a seven-day grace period for storage fees according to previous regulations. After that, the fee is 0.015 yuan per ton per day. Yesterday, the Miscellaneous Grain Association suddenly issued an announcement stating that it had received a letter from the stationmaster of McGruer Road stating that according to a telegram from the Vehicle Affairs Office, starting this month, the new regulations for storage fees would be implemented. The new regulations state that goods arriving at the station have a five-day grace period, and after that, the fee is 0.05 yuan per ton per day for a full carload. If the carload is less than a ton, the fee is 0.01 yuan per 50 kilograms. According to this, the fee will increase threefold compared to the previous regulations, which will likely have a significant impact on future market prices. The industry must hold a meeting immediately to discuss this.

Large Quantities of Flour Transported to Guandong

In the past two weeks, the quantity of flour transported from this port to Guandong has reached more than 100,000 bags. The reason for this is that the weather has been getting colder recently, and Andong, Yingkou, and other places are at risk of icing over. Once frozen, waterway transportation will be blocked until the spring, when it will recover. During this icy period, merchants must prepare goods and food in advance to supply the market. Therefore, Northern foreign guest merchants stationed in Shanghai are rushing to transport goods, with flour being the main item. It is reported that there will be another 180,000 bags of flour loaded on two ships to be transported to Yingkou today. It is estimated that there will be another 100,000 bags waiting to be transported next week.

The U.S. dollar is expected to fluctuate again soon. Moreover, with no resolution in sight for the labor strike at New York silk mills, the raw silk market has collapsed. Coupled with the strengthening of the U.S. dollar, the prices for Chinese raw silk are increasingly low. While Grade B white filature silk can still fetch $1.50 (U.S.) per pound, the equivalent price in Chinese currency is only over 550 yuan per bale. The prospects for Chinese raw silk sales to the U.S. are becoming increasingly bleak.

(Over Three Hundred Pieces of Silk Waste Shipped to France) The French postal ship "Isles" departed yesterday, carrying a total of three hundred and eighty-three pieces of white silk waste from various local silk businesses, destined for Marseilles, Angers, and other ports.

(Large Quantities of Artificial Silk Shipped Inland) The artificial silk that various local "Zhun Xing" firms should have turned over to Chinese merchants last month is now being shipped out in batches. In the past three days alone, shipments of American artificial silk via water routes to Qingdao, Tianjin, Hangzhou, Huzhou, Jiaxing, and various ports along the Yangtze River have reached 738 cases.

(Foreign Firms' Silk Market Has Reached an Impasse) Overseas markets have been unsettled by unfavorable rumors circulating in Washington, leading to foreign exchange instability. New York and Lyon have ample silk inventories, and silk trading has become illiquid. Yokohama's Japanese raw silk prices have plummeted drastically, reaching new lows. Foreign firms in Shanghai are adopting a wait-and-see approach, and silk sales have reached an impasse. Yesterday, only twenty-seven bales of grey and yellow silk were traded, with prices remaining weak and flat.
